    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText1757747902490799318" style="display:none">What happens when you're stalked by Death? You fall in love with him, of course.<br /><br />Pagan Moore doesn't cheat Death, but instead, falls in love with him.<br /><br />Seventeen year old Pagan Moore has seen souls her entire life. Once she realized the strangers she often saw walking through walls were not visible to anyone else, she started ignoring them. If she didn't let them know she could see them, then they left her alone. Until she stepped out of her car the first day of school and saw an incredibly sexy guy lounging on a picnic table, watching her with an amused smirk on his face. Problem is, she knows he's dead.<br /><br />Not only does he not go away when she ignores him, but he does something none of the others have ever done. He speaks. Pagan is fascinated by the soul. What she doesn't realize is that her appointed time to die is drawing near and the wickedly beautiful soul she is falling in love with is not a soul at all.<br /><br />He is Death and he's about to break all the rules.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1854592627154688306"><b>My thoughts before reading the book</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>What happens when you're stalked by Death? You fall in love with him, of course.</i>
</blockquote><br/>Oh god, why am I going to read this???<br/><br/>*looks at the cover model's eyes*<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380358781ra/709958.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Yes master... I shall read the book...<br/><br/><br/><b>My thoughts while reading the book</b><br/><br/>▪ Pagan? What kind of name is Pagan?<br/><br/>▪ Of course he’s gorgeous, just look at that damn cover!!<br/><br/>▪ Ugh please don’t let it be a love triangle!!<br/><br/>▪ Give me more of the dead dude.<br/><br/>▪ Fair hair for the good guy dark hair for the evil one? Typical. I</span>
  <span id="freeText1854592627154688306" style="display:none"><b>My thoughts before reading the book</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>What happens when you're stalked by Death? You fall in love with him, of course.</i>
</blockquote><br>Oh god, why am I going to read this???<br><br>*looks at the cover model's eyes*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380358781ra/709958.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes master... I shall read the book...<br><br><br><b>My thoughts while reading the book</b><br><br>▪ Pagan? What kind of name is Pagan?<br><br>▪ Of course he’s gorgeous, just look at that damn cover!!<br><br>▪ Ugh please don’t let it be a love triangle!!<br><br>▪ Give me more of the dead dude.<br><br>▪ Fair hair for the good guy dark hair for the evil one? Typical. Is this why I have a thing for dark haired men?<br><br>▪ Meeeh love triangle ಠ_ಠ <br><br>▪ She ended in the nuthouse. How fitting.<br><br>▪ The ending = barf.<br><br><br><b>My thoughts after finishing the book [and after taking my anger out on my blind neighbor]</b><br><br>This could have been so much better. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380358781ra/709959.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358781i/709960.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, yeah, you’re right. It couldn’t have been better..<br><br>Everyone’s boring in this book; they have no personality whatsoever. When Pagan speaks I feel like I’m listening to a thirty year old woman and not a teenager. Not that a thirty year old woman would always be boring. I know some than are more immature than a sixteen year old. But that’s beside the point. Pagan is boring, Leif is super boring and Miranda is a desperate girl drooling over anything that has a penis. Dank is the only one standing out. Because he’s meant to stand out. Compared to the rest of the characters his presence is like Lady Gaga attending an award show.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358782i/709961.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you don’t know what I mean then read on my friend.. Read on..<br><br>Dank is too exaggerated because he freakin’ stands out too much. And, oh noo, guess what? He’s Death. I mean Death aka The Reaper.<br><br>Bitch please. <br><br>Death. A teenager. That happens to be in a rock band. Who falls in love with an insignificant teenager. Twilight much? What, vampires are not popular anymore so Abbi Glines said <i>”What the hell? The formula seems to work so why not Google some creature, make him hot as hell and- oh wait. Hell. The Devil! No, no, that’s too much.. Everyone sees Al Pacino as the Devil. He’s not sexy enough. Oooh, I could die for an idea right now! Wait! Die! That’s it! I’ll make him Death! But not the black caped creepy skeleton thing but a sexy model like guy. Oooh, Ian Somerhalder but younger and even hotter! Brilliant!”</i><br><br>No Mrs. Glines, it’s not brilliant. It’s bullshit.<br><br><br><b>My thoughts on the next book in the series</b><br><br>Barf.</span>

I have to say that I really enjoyed Existence. The only thing I didn't like about it was the fact that Pagan had a boyfriend that wasn't the hero the whole book. Leif on the other hand was too good to be true. For some reason he rubbed me the wrong way and I don't like or trust him. I liked the budding love between Dank and Pagan. <div id="review_1379300365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379300365" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1379300365?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=para-dystopian-sci-fi-fantasy">para-dystopian-sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=author-abbi-glines">author-abbi-glines</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1379300365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12050363099666166036"><b>4.5 <i>”It is appointed.”</i> Stars</b><br/><br/><span>[image error]</span> <br/><br/>Being an Abbi Glines fan, I realized that I have read all her books but this series. Who isn’t interested in seeing what Abbi can do with a paranormal storyline? Going in, I thought I was getting another gorgeous teen girl in cut off shorts and tiny tops with a bunch of issues falling for some sort of para entity, but Abbi Glines surprised me! <br/><br/>Pagan Moore is a great heroine, nothing like the heroines in her other books and the storyline while based in he</span>
  <span id="freeText12050363099666166036" style="display:none"><b>4.5 <i>”It is appointed.”</i> Stars</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span> <br><br>Being an Abbi Glines fan, I realized that I have read all her books but this series. Who isn’t interested in seeing what Abbi can do with a paranormal storyline? Going in, I thought I was getting another gorgeous teen girl in cut off shorts and tiny tops with a bunch of issues falling for some sort of para entity, but Abbi Glines surprised me! <br><br>Pagan Moore is a great heroine, nothing like the heroines in her other books and the storyline while based in her senior year of high school was totally not predictable!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492279530ra/22501729.gif" width="390" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Pagan can see lost souls bumping around our world but she can't talk to them. She doesn’t cross them over, she just pretends she doesn’t see anything because there’s nothing for her to do for them. Until the day that a hot guy soul actually speaks to her and the Harbor High’s star quarterback asks for her help with his speech class.<br><br>Pagan finds herself drawn to Dank Walker and things get even crazier when he makes his presence known at school and it turns out he’s a rock star?? <br><br><b>
  <i>”I can’t tell you what I am. I’ve broken enough rules already.”</i>
</b><br><br>There’s action and the good type of drama as Pagan struggles with her feelings for Dank and her safe relationship with sweet Leif.<br><br><b>
  <i>”Why couldn’t I love him instead?”</i>
</b><br><br>What a dilmena! The story does end with an<b> AWESOME</b> cliffhanger and so this reader is onto the next book with great anticipation as to what is to come for this well constructed love triangle of SOULS!! <br><br><b>
  <i>”I’m not a man so I do not have a heart that loves as a human does. I’m an immortal god that dwells with supreme power because I hold the keys to death. But you are my existence. I am yours.”</i>
</b><br><br>I’m so glad I gave this book a go because friends ratings are everywhere from one star to five star reviews. The ending has me ignoring today's new releases and jumping right into book two! <br></span>

<div id="review_343649301" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343649301" />
    <a title="Kandise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4606975-kandise"><img alt="Kandise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351466626p2/4606975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343649301?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandise" href="/user/show/4606975-kandise">Kandise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4606975-kandise?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4606975-kandise?shelf=quick-reads-under-200-pgs">quick-reads-under-200-pgs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343649301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6876157904758614342">I’m completely dumbfounded that this book has so far rated at an average of 4.01 stars…<br/> <br/>Pagan is a selfish and mentally unstable bitch. I wanted to slap her, slap the holy living shit right out of her face. <br/><br/>So she sees souls and it has been like that since she was a wee babe, but they don’t usually speak to her except for the gorgeous guy with awesome blue eyes and black dreamy hair. Yeah, he talks to her and he sings for her and she is already feeling this kid, like <i>yeah</i> but she knows that even</span>
  <span id="freeText6876157904758614342" style="display:none">I’m completely dumbfounded that this book has so far rated at an average of 4.01 stars…<br /> <br />Pagan is a selfish and mentally unstable bitch. I wanted to slap her, slap the holy living shit right out of her face. <br /><br />So she sees souls and it has been like that since she was a wee babe, but they don’t usually speak to her except for the gorgeous guy with awesome blue eyes and black dreamy hair. Yeah, he talks to her and he sings for her and she is already feeling this kid, like <i>yeah</i> but she knows that even though she is attracted to him, that she can’t ever really be with him because he isn’t real, so she does the sane thing and gets a boyfriend, Leif.<br /><br />Then Dank (what the hell kind of name is that anyway?) manifests into a real life boy! Hence the beginning of shameless Pagan; she stares at him, she steals quick glances across the lunchroom and she has the nerve to get mad that he is chatting up the high school floozy…all while her BOYFRIEND is sitting right next to her with his hands on her hips! She doesn’t even care! And to top it off, she only gives a fleeting thought to whether or not she should break up with him! Why? Oh because he was “normal”…so she just strings him along.<br /><br />Ok, so let me part with this piece of sage advice: Just because you admit you’re being a bitch doesn’t make it right..or make you less of a bitch. You are still a bitch. You are still a raging bitch. Got it? Ok, let's move on.<br /><br />Then the pièce de résistance! She gets herself admitted into a mental hospital! Yes!<b> A MENTAL HOSPITAL!</b> Because SHE LOVES DANK TOO MUCH and she can’t have him and now he is ignoring her after their makeout session, which by the way happened at prom when she was there with LEIF, then she had the balls to make her date drive her home and let him believe it was his fault she was in such a pissy mood…with pouty face and all. Bitch. Oh and the hole, that grand canyon sized hole on her heart is just so immense, she just can’t take being without Dank, she can’t eat or breath and life needs to just end (boo hoo!) and yet she still doesn’t end it with Leif. That's right, she lets him come and visit her at the institution, she even holds his hand and nuzzles her nose in his neck knowing damn well that she doesn’t feel anything for him. Effing Bitch. <br /><br />Ooo Ooo, best part? When the Psychiatrist tells her that she doesn’t belong at the institution because she is normal and healthy…<i>What?!</i> She belonged in that institution dummy! Sitting right next to that Southern country bumpkin stereotype!<br /><br />Oh but wait though, she then has the audacity to try and kill herself for Dank! You may now begin to wonder if she even gave a second thought to the other people in her life. Let me save you the effort, NO, she didn’t. Dank is all she cared about, she was going to just disappear off the face of the Earth for a guy that she had known for roughly, <i>ehhh</i> 2 minutes? <br /><br />Are you feeling the warm and fuzzies yet?<br /><br />Cause if you didn’t already, the ending will get ya and I’m not talking about the “twist”. I’m talking about the bitch tearing out of the school without a second glance to her boyfriend while she makes out with another dude 2 feet away from the school entrance without any shame…just shameless.<br /><br />And was that “twist” supposed to make me feel better about how she treated Leif? Cause it didn’t. <br /><br /><b>Bottom line:</b> It was just too much over the top drama. That most definitely wasn’t love; it was a chemical imbalance that requires medication. Pagan you need medication.<br /><br />But I'm going to read the second installment, cause I want to know what's up with my man. I don't know why exactly seeing as my WTS was in full effect and I was at a level 9 with the ERS, but I want to know what Leif does to make her life shitty, because I wont hold it against him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6876157904758614342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_240140580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240140580" />
    <a title="Kelly Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6770174-kelly-martin"><img alt="Kelly Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448333255p2/6770174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240140580?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Martin" href="/user/show/6770174-kelly-martin">Kelly Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240140580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9515192618499330576">First, for lack of a better phrase, Dank is hotness incarnate. This is quite possibly the hottest, sexiest, steamiest YA book boyfriend I've ever read.<br/><br/>Second, Dank? I literally smacked myself in the forehead with my Kindle when I realized oh, that's not a typo, THAT'S HIS NAME. To each his own, I guess.<br/><br/>You know how they say don't judge a book by it's cover? With this one, go ahead, it's ok. It's what originally drew me to the book, so kudos to whoever's responsible for that little gift of gorgeo</span>
  <span id="freeText9515192618499330576" style="display:none">First, for lack of a better phrase, Dank is hotness incarnate. This is quite possibly the hottest, sexiest, steamiest YA book boyfriend I've ever read.<br /><br />Second, Dank? I literally smacked myself in the forehead with my Kindle when I realized oh, that's not a typo, THAT'S HIS NAME. To each his own, I guess.<br /><br />You know how they say don't judge a book by it's cover? With this one, go ahead, it's ok. It's what originally drew me to the book, so kudos to whoever's responsible for that little gift of gorgeous. I'm not surprised to find out it's probably the same duo that graces the cover of Jennifer Armentrout's Lux series, who have caused quite the stir. Thank you, from the bottom of my heart, whoever started this list <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/15049.That_Girl_Hot_Guy_from_the_Obsidian_Cover" rel="nofollow noopener">That Girl and Hot Guy from the Obsidian Cover</a> &lt;3<br /><br />The story was different, interesting, well thought out and not quite what I expected, but the end somewhat confusing. Is this part of a series? Because it seemed a bit cliffhangerish at the end and I would have been REALLY confused had I not read the little prequel from Death's PoV. <br /><br />***Do yourself a favor and seriously, stop reading if you haven't finished the book, because this is going to get hard core spoilery and take it from someone who always reads the last paqe first, you'll want to be surprised.***<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But even having read that prequel, and assuming I'm correct in thinking Leif was the "soulless" Death saw when he first met Pagan, it still doesn't explain who sent him and why. And are we ever going to find out what she has to do to become immortal? Or for that matter, why her soul is weird? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It kept my interest enough that I stayed up all night to finish, and I only spent a fraction of that time gazing stupidly at the pretty cover.<br /><br />***Edit: they now have it listed as part of a Trilogy, which explains soooo much~! Also, hell yeah, I can't wait for book 2.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9515192618499330576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer242043807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9257775623389478924">Girl meets stalker.<br/>*Insert a couple of angry exchanges here*<br/>Stalker stops coming round like he used to. <br/>Girl misses stalker.<br/><br/>This is the part where something big and *cough* unexpected *cough* happens.. oh say, a near-death experience where stalker steps in and saves the day.<br/><br/>Stalker takes this time to insinuate himself into <s>girl's</s> Pagan's life; his name we now learn is Dank. Yes, that's right, Dank. <br/>Sexy.<br/><br/><s>Stalker</s> Dank is a popular fellow. He seemingly enjoys the attention of the queen bitch of Pag</span>
  <span id="freeText9257775623389478924" style="display:none">Girl meets stalker.<br />*Insert a couple of angry exchanges here*<br />Stalker stops coming round like he used to. <br />Girl misses stalker.<br /><br />This is the part where something big and *cough* unexpected *cough* happens.. oh say, a near-death experience where stalker steps in and saves the day.<br /><br />Stalker takes this time to insinuate himself into <s>girl's</s> Pagan's life; his name we now learn is Dank. Yes, that's right, Dank. <br />Sexy.<br /><br /><s>Stalker</s> Dank is a popular fellow. He seemingly enjoys the attention of the queen bitch of Pagan's school, all the while outwardly ignoring her but tossing an occasional enigmatic offering to the poor confused girl.<br /><br />The plot thickens. Dank claims he's not what Pagan thinks he is. He tells her to run away, far, far away from him. And her response?<br /><i>“I don’t care what you are,” I said, taking a step toward him. “You can’t scare me off and I’m not running away.</i><br />Hmmm…that sounded strangely familiar...<br /><br />There was even the obligatory preppy love-struck puppy who the girl is determined to be with because he's so <i>real</i> and he makes her feel so <i>safe</i>.<br /><br />Not once did I feel like I was engaging with the characters of this book. <i>Dank</i>, at the very least, should have been engaging. He's death! <br />I have loved the idea of personifying death ever since I read The Book Thief and I was really looking forward to this book, but it just fell flat. <br />As for the romance between him and Pagan…stalking a girl, flashing hot and cold with her, dropping mysterious comments while warning her off of you is a recipe for romance I could really do with seeing less of. Looking back, they can't have exchanged more than a few sentences but there you have it, insta-love. *sigh*<br /><br />I'm giving this book two stars, mainly because I try to reserve the one star rating for books that I actively dislike but, like I said, I was really looking forward to this book and.. it was a disappointment to say the least.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9257775623389478924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237249313" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237249313" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237249313?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=reapers-necromancers-death-agents">reapers-necromancers-death-agents</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237249313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9662279755801732306"><b>Review Revision 04/12 to add alternate PoV (Dank). GR is not showing a listing for the alternate, so I'm adding it to this review because the story ties to book 1</b><br/><br/>Even though the alternate PoV covered several scenes from <i>Existence</i>, it was not a full length book. Think of this as a highlight reel.<br/><br/>It's too bad the entire (original) book wasn't written in Dank's PoV because he was more interesting to read. I can't say that I'm surprised. These days I'm finding myself drawn to male protags because th</span>
  <span id="freeText9662279755801732306" style="display:none"><b>Review Revision 04/12 to add alternate PoV (Dank). GR is not showing a listing for the alternate, so I'm adding it to this review because the story ties to book 1</b><br><br>Even though the alternate PoV covered several scenes from <i>Existence</i>, it was not a full length book. Think of this as a highlight reel.<br><br>It's too bad the entire (original) book wasn't written in Dank's PoV because he was more interesting to read. I can't say that I'm surprised. These days I'm finding myself drawn to male protags because they're able to dial back some of the obsessive intensity without losing the emotion completely. I wasn't 100% sold on Dank's voice as sounding male but I much preferred being inside of his head over being in Pagan's.<br><br><b>Dank, you're not half bad...</b><br><i>I let my eyes travel down her dress and enjoyed the simple fact that she'd bought it for me. I'd suggested this color. The dress hadn't been bought for the quarterback. The need to growl my approval was overwhelming.</i><br><br>This one's a bit spoilerish if you haven't read <i>Existence</i> yet, so read at your own risk. I will say that this one spoiler made me ache for Dank even more than I did.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>Then I recognized the danger. Her soul was releasing from her body. With each hungry touch from Death she relinquished herself to me. Terror washed over me as I jerked out of her embrace and stepped back. "I can't, Pagan. I want this so damn bad. But I can't." Before she could stop me, I fled.</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The alternate PoV was a huge improvement over the original book itself but there wasn't enough content for me to want to raise the star rating on my original review. However, it does make me a little more hopeful about book 2.<br><br>I mentioned in my <i>Existence</i> review that Pagan and Dank have to be some of the worst names ever. On the cover of Existence, you have a couple of glorious models (who happen to be all over the place right now on a multitude of various stock book covers). Aren't they beautiful? <i>Do these people look like a Pagan and a Dank?</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363425i/714786.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I didn't think so either. When I think of Pagan and Dank, this is more the image that comes to mind.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363425i/714787.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Who's with me here?<br><br><b>Original Review for Existence - 02/12</b><br><br>2.5 stars. I had a very hard time getting past the names Pagan and Dank. With all the names in the world, this was what we got stuck with? When I read the following sentence in the book, I swear I read the name as <i>Dank Wanker</i> at first (I wish I was kidding) : <i>The soul, my soul, was Dank Walker the rocker?</i> Hmmm...Walker. Let's see - Walker the Rocker. Yes, that's much better. Argh.<br><br><i>Before I veer off into a possibly cranky rant about what I didn't like about this book, let me say what I did like. </i><br><br>I like stories where Death is an actual character. Who wouldn't want to see Death in action?<br><br>I liked watching Death's internal struggle when you could tell he wasn't having an easy time letting go of what he knew he needed to. His little possessive growls were kind of sexy.<br><br>I liked the end, and not because the book itself came to an end and I was ready to be done. I actually liked the plot twist and setup for book 2, even though I guessed what was coming very early on in the story. This book may have not been anything to write home about in the first half, but I found myself having a lot of fun reading the second half. If the next book in the series gets better, I could easily see myself going up a full star or two on the rating. This type of book has a good concept and good bones...we're just drowning a bit in some of the writing that could stand to be taken down a notch.<br><br><i>Now on to what I didn't like.</i><br><br>The name thing, as witnessed by my opening paragraph.<br><br>Most of the first half of the book. I didn't connect to any character at all, other than Death (Dank Wanker).<br><br>The sappiness was done in such a way that it was bordering on cheese. The "you are my reason for existence" spiel was painful to read. I am a huge fan of love stories and romance, so you know something's got to be off when even I'm having to fight wanting to put a fake 'finger gun' to my head and fake 'pull the trigger.'<br><br>The love duo/triangle/square/WTF is this thing? I am not a hater of love triangles and will not automatically write off a book which has one, but if there's going to be one, it needs to be worth the read. One of the love interests had the appeal of a box of stale cereal. From what I can tell, the triangle might be dead now, so here's hoping. *cross fingers*<br><br>Case in point about the love triangle - it's probably time to call it quits with one of the people you're hooking up with, when someone is able to observe this :<br><br><i>"The emotion he evokes in you is not strong. There is only comfort, not passion, running through your thoughts when he holds you."</i><br><br>Believe it or not, even with my complaints about the first half, I did enjoy the second half of the book, even to the point where I'm sincerely (no sarcasm here) looking forward to the next book. Once the story finally got to a point where I was interested, I started to enjoy where it was going. The "looney bin" and following scenes were entertaining to read. We might even get rewarded with some good conflict or fight scenes in book 2 if the end of book 1 is any indication. If so, you might even see me break out a tentative happy dance.<br><br>Before you decide whether or not to read <i>Existence</i>, I'd first ask what you're looking for in a book. If you prefer your romances more subtle when it comes to declarations of undying devotion, this probably isn't the book for you. Fans of 'true love conquers all' stories will probably enjoy the book. I'd have an easy time recommending this one to a few friends who I know love books which have a protective hero type, or who I know like themes in which love seems to be the driving motivation of why people make the decisions that they do.<br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9662279755801732306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10676775812693162275">1.5 stars - Spoilers beware<br/>Another YA book with the same old formula.. why do I keep punishing myself reading books like these..because I keep hoping that I'll find characters that I'll fall in love with even if the story maybe similar to every other paranormal YA book.<br/>Anyway we have our protagonist Pagan who can see souls/ghosts.. but can't communicate with them.   <span id="freeText10676775812693162275" style="display:none">1.5 stars - Spoilers beware<br />Another YA book with the same old formula.. why do I keep punishing myself reading books like these..because I keep hoping that I'll find characters that I'll fall in love with even if the story maybe similar to every other paranormal YA book.<br />Anyway we have our protagonist Pagan who can see souls/ghosts.. but can't communicate with them. One day she sees a soul/ghost who talks to her.. needless to say she's shocked.. and also fascinated by his oh so beautiful beauty.. <br />Pagan is weak, she cries, moans, breaks down, runs away every chance she gets. She starts to tutor the highschool quarterback - Leif and for some strange reason Leif likes her and starts to date her - maybe he hurt his head at a football game and lost his senses.. who knows. Anyways Leif and Pagan become closer but the beautiful soul - who wait for is called Dank- WTF?? turns up at her school as a student and starts flirting with Kendra, Leif's ex.. of course Pagan is heartbroken that he's flirting with Kendra who she labels as the 'school slut' which just makes her seem bitchy. <br />Leif is a good boyf but Pagan doesn't appreciate him and just pines for our dear Dank - the only reason I can think of for her pining after him is that he's hot and plays her music, oh and he's wrote her a lullaby a la Edward and Bella. <br />Pagan finds out that Dank is actually Death and he saved her life when she should have died.. Pagan loves him now more than ever, but still doesn't break up with Leif.. Dank goes away to protect her.. blah blah blah.. Pagan has a breakdown because Dank said bye bye and ends up in a mental hospital because she's a weak, self pitying, self centred fool.. Leif is there for her.. Pagan still doesn't break up with him.. stuff happens.. more stuff happens.. Dank and Pagan kiss and make up.. and then she finally decides she should break up with Leif of course after she's kissed and declared her love to Dank.. the last line we find out Leif's not human?!!! so because of the last line I must read the next book to find out what my favourite character is.. sigh.. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458270952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9924309313355217195"><i>Negative stars. Will a fart suffice?</i><br/><br/>I'm calling it: BULLSHIT.<br/><br/>4.01 stars??? <br/><br/>Pfft.<br/><br/>This book was awful. Completely awful. <br/><br/>The writing sounded like a tween took a part of a dream that lasted three minutes and tried to spin it into a book. Then some really awful publisher, the kind that secretly hates literacy, published it in its unedited, repetitious glory. <br/><br/>Also the book mostly only uses two sassytime adjectives: growl and shiver. As in, "He growled" and "I shivered". No, lie. I wouldn't lie to you</span>
  <span id="freeText9924309313355217195" style="display:none"><i>Negative stars. Will a fart suffice?</i><br /><br />I'm calling it: BULLSHIT.<br /><br />4.01 stars??? <br /><br />Pfft.<br /><br />This book was awful. Completely awful. <br /><br />The writing sounded like a tween took a part of a dream that lasted three minutes and tried to spin it into a book. Then some really awful publisher, the kind that secretly hates literacy, published it in its unedited, repetitious glory. <br /><br />Also the book mostly only uses two sassytime adjectives: growl and shiver. As in, "He growled" and "I shivered". No, lie. I wouldn't lie to you like that.<br /><br />Lets start with our protagonist Pagan because really no one else matters:<br /><br />She is the worst kind of selfish bitch. The story begins with her being judgmental to the hot kid because well, he's hot, duh. He then melts her super mature exterior and she starts to date him. Then, then, watch closely now, she proceeds to squat over his super hot self and rain the worst kind of super-D-duper, molten lava, shit all over him for the remainder of the book. <br /><br />She is manipulative. She is a liar. She is so shallow she's basically non existent. She has the typical YA disease of the Me-Me's. <b>Exhibit A:</b> While she was exhibiting profoundly annoying behavior, from pages 15 to 162, she would say things like "I feel bad" but she really fucking did not because she just kept on keeping on. <b>Exhibit B: </b> Everything in her world was "Me". "<i> I </i> can't <i> live</i> without him!!", "<i> My</i> heart has a hole in it", "<i>I</i> don't care who I hurt to get/keep him!", "<i>I</i> don't love this kid that loves me, treats me so well, takes on guilt because he thinks he's causing my shitty behavior when he's not but I'm going to use him for comfort" And that my friends was the worst one. <b>Exhibit C:</b> She does something she thinks is soooooooooo romantically "sacrificial" but it's really just her not being to wrap her immature mind around anything past the space that is two inches in front of her nose. Disgusting. <br /><br />Leif: What was the point of Leif? Was it just so Abbikins could stretch this wretch of material not fit to wipe my ass into three or more books? Because that's what I'm smelling. You don't get to write a lovely character such as Leif, make him the punching bag all book long and then <i> dum-dum-dum</i> leave a "cliffhanger" that's supposed to, what, excuse Pagans shit-tastic behavior?? No sell. No goddamn sell, That girl was straight up asshole and you know it.<br /><br />Dank: <i>WHAT?</i> For starters what in Sam Hill is a <i> Dank?</i> It sounds like it smells wet. I.e.: The rain sure is bringing out a dank smell. See? It doesn't sound like it smells good. <br /><br />What was the point of that part close to the end? You know what I'm talking about, Peggy Ann. Oh, you know. Was it so the author could reinforce that we were in fact supposed to like the protagonist? We were supposed to remember the qualities about her that we long since forgot when she went super C-U-Next-Tuesday? Again, no sell.<br /><br />All in All: Boo. Super Boo. The writing was awful and Pagan ruined everything.<br /><br />P.S. People who live on farms have freckles, buck teeth, speak unintelligently and have stringy hair. #Truth. I was unaware that that was widely known but as they say: you learn something new everyday.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9924309313355217195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3647721055714158404">Ahhhh! Abbi!!! What are you doing to me with that ending! Gah.<br/>Ok, I officially want a Dank! ;) And a Leif.<br/>I worried about this book. I'm not into love triangles, but aye! I love them both. Abbi made this story work, which is really hard to do with a love triangle for me.   <span id="freeText3647721055714158404" style="display:none">Ahhhh! Abbi!!! What are you doing to me with that ending! Gah.<br />Ok, I officially want a Dank! ;) And a Leif.<br />I worried about this book. I'm not into love triangles, but aye! I love them both. I usually dont read books less the 300 pages because to me you can't get a good story and a plot down in anything less but existence pleasantly surprised me. I am a fan of abbi's writing and this is my favorite of them all! She has a way of getting to the point of the subject in a few paragraphs and has good sized chapters. The characters are lovable and easy to like. The hole "death" finds love pulls you in and keeps you reading. It's a quick, easy and </span>
  <span id="freeText10970715743651974955" style="display:none"><br /> <br /> I really like existence by abbi glines. I am a fan of abbi's writing and this is my favorite of them all! She has a way of getting to the point of the subject in a few paragraphs and has good sized chapters. The characters are lovable and easy to like. The hole "death" finds love pulls you in and keeps you reading. It's a quick, easy and fun read and I defiantly would recommend it. I give it a 5/5 stars :) </span>

<div id="review_525520169" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/525520169" />
    <a title="Sammi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192860-sammi"><img alt="Sammi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431972159p2/8192860.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sammi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sammi" href="/user/show/8192860-sammi">Sammi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192860-sammi?shelf=thought-would-be-better">thought-would-be-better</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192860-sammi?shelf=own-on-kindle">own-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192860-sammi?shelf=ew-love-triangle">ew-love-triangle</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer525520169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9226755423154444800">OH MY GOD YOU HAVE TO BE KIDDING ME? I ran with this book trying to be forgiving, I kept telling myself not to be so spiteful and hateful toward it as I <i>believed</i> this was self published. I mean… if grammar was a living, breathing person, I’m pretty sure he would go and jump off a cliff after reading this. <br/><br/>But really??? Someone read this and decided to publish it? I’m pretty sure the family cat could have done a better job at editing. For example… is it really necessary to say three times in a pa</span>
  <span id="freeText9226755423154444800" style="display:none">OH MY GOD YOU HAVE TO BE KIDDING ME? I ran with this book trying to be forgiving, I kept telling myself not to be so spiteful and hateful toward it as I <i>believed</i> this was self published. I mean… if grammar was a living, breathing person, I’m pretty sure he would go and jump off a cliff after reading this. <br><br>But really??? Someone read this and decided to publish it? I’m pretty sure the family cat could have done a better job at editing. For example… is it really necessary to say three times in a paragraph how someone’s eyes made her feel? There was just SO much waffle.<br><br>Don’t even get me started on the characters names…. Pagan, Leif &amp; <b>Dank?????</b> Wth kinda name is that? It doesn’t say <i>mysterious, sexy, intriguing or death</i> … it makes him sounds like a problem you’d have at home with leaky pipes. <b>“Honey, the pipes have burst, we have Dank in the basement again.”</b><br><br>So lets start on Pagan…. She’s a moany, whiney, selfish, bitchy waste of space. Through pretty much this whole book she’s seeing this guy called Leif, star quarterback and really good boyfriend, sweet, kind &amp; thoughtful. Pagan decides she doesn’t love him and she only has eyes for Dank. However she decides to string him along for the whole story. She uses him to make herself feel better and the poor guy doesn’t have a clue. This is the same girl who actually has the gall to call another girl ‘Kendra’ the school slut? Pfft. At least she’s honest instead of trying to pretend she’s a timid, good little girl. <br><br>I was genuinely going to rate this as a 1* …I have only rated this as 2* due to the last 2 chapters. Its just a shame Pagan didn’t actually die and end of this selfish farce. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408005ra/797684.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>You can also find my reviews here: <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://lilythenovelnerd.wordpress.com/">http://lilythenovelnerd.wordpress.com/</a> (tho they are alot more colourful)<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9226755423154444800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer417123122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10513613574197873193"><b>Brief summary</b><br/>Pagan sees souls that wander the earth. She ignores them until she meets a boy named Dank, who is the first soul to ever speak to her. She knows something is different about him, but she can't figure out what it is. Things get even more confusing for Pagan when Dank is suddenly a student at her school that everyone can see.<br/><br/><b>What I liked</b><br/>This is a unique story. I read a lot of young adult paranormal books and this is one type that I don't come across very often. I thought I knew what w</span>
  <span id="freeText10513613574197873193" style="display:none"><b>Brief summary</b><br />Pagan sees souls that wander the earth. She ignores them until she meets a boy named Dank, who is the first soul to ever speak to her. She knows something is different about him, but she can't figure out what it is. Things get even more confusing for Pagan when Dank is suddenly a student at her school that everyone can see.<br /><br /><b>What I liked</b><br />This is a unique story. I read a lot of young adult paranormal books and this is one type that I don't come across very often. I thought I knew what was going to happen next, but I was wrong a number of times and that was refreshing too. I did know what Dank is, but that's about all I guessed correctly.<br /><br /><b>What I didn't like</b> <br />There were a few things I wished were different. I wasn't a fan of the names of the main characters. I think I understand why she used the name "Dank", but it was odd enough to distract me from the story every time I read it. The middle kind of dragged a bit and it bothered me how much Pagan used Leif.<br /><br /><b>Brief thoughts</b><br /><i>Existence</i> is a decent read. The last 20% of the book was really good and I was completely shocked by the last sentence (I really, really did NOT see that coming!). I was planning on reading book 2 before I reached the end anyhow, but that last sentence made me want to start <i>Predestined</i> now.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5009396792997762198" style="display:none">Yes, this cover does Death justice. Every time his eyes are mentioned, remember the cover and swoon. This book has the feel of an Abbi Glines romance with a shift to the paranormal. <br /><br />Overall: I enjoyed this book very much. I read it within two night sittings and couldn’t wait to keep reading. Book one, to me, feels like more of a YA love story with paranormal elements, because the plot doesn’t revolve around paranormal activity like other paranormal romance books I’ve read. Glines can write some romance, that’s for sure! However, we haven’t reached the full plot or what is really going on yet in this story overall. I think there is more to some of these characters and story than we learn in book one. I’m looking forward to the sequel!<br /><br />You can read my full review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ataleofmanyreviews.com/index.php/2011/11/existence-by-abbi-glines/">http://www.ataleofmanyreviews.com/ind...</a><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer482090223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17260746533949706428">I hated this book. Hated hated hated it. It's dull, stupid, sexist, and as appealing and enjoyable as a bad case of PMS. I only chose to read this book because of the gorgeous guy on the cover. Sigh. I'm a fool for a pretty face, and a pretty cover. And once again, my love for superficial beauty bites me in the ass.<br/><br/>At least I didn't spend any money on this crap. And since I skimmed it (and its sequel), I didn't waste too much of this time. <br/><br/>I can't think of anything positive to say about this nov</span>
  <span id="freeText17260746533949706428" style="display:none">I hated this book. Hated hated hated it. It's dull, stupid, sexist, and as appealing and enjoyable as a bad case of PMS. I only chose to read this book because of the gorgeous guy on the cover. Sigh. I'm a fool for a pretty face, and a pretty cover. And once again, my love for superficial beauty bites me in the ass.<br /><br />At least I didn't spend any money on this crap. And since I skimmed it (and its sequel), I didn't waste too much of this time. <br /><br />I can't think of anything positive to say about this novel, other than that at least it wasn't as offensive as Hush Hush or Twilight. Dank (wtf kind of name is that?) is obsessive and clearly mentally unstable, but at least he doesn't cause physical harm to the MC. It's not as materialistic as <i>Switched</i>, nor as dull and lazily written as <i>Firelight</i>.<br /><br />Seriously bitchy (and spoiler-y) review follows under the spoiler. This novel pissed me off just that much. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Instead of writing a conventional review, I decided to write a recipe for writing a shitty paranormal romance YA novel like this one, to properly express my love for baking and my disdain for this novel:<br /><br />- Take one female protagonist. Give her a personality bypass. Make her whiny, utterly lacking in intelligence or determination, and a jerk to her friends and family. For good measure, add a large dose of sexism and double standards. "Slut" should be a regular part of her vocabulary. She's dark-haired and hates all blonde girls. She's stunningly gorgeous but thinks she's plain. An ordinary name like Emily or Shannon or even a more exotic name like Skye or Brianna or Ebony won't do. She has to have an utterly ridiculous Mary-Sue name: Pagan.<br /><br />- Take one tall, dark, and handsome male love interest. Make him hot, but <i>mysterious</i>. Actually, <i>mysterious</i> is just a code word for <i>dick</i>. Make him jealous, possessive, selfish, and hypocritical. He goes through girls like toilet paper and treats the protagonist like a child. Although he stays as pure as the driven snow while he dates a girl he doesn't even like (it's not really explained, but it seems like it's to make Pagan jealous) and uses every girl he's with, he 's just a sexy hottie, the girls he's with are branded as "sluts", "whores", "bitches". This might make him unpalatable, but don't worry, YA readers will eat that shit up so long as he's good-looking. Again, give him a ridiculous name, like "Dank" (it means damp and musty, how ROMANTIC). Don't bother to explain his supernatural powers, his backstory, give him interests or a personality or motives beyond hormones. Who cares about telling a good story?<br /><br />- Take one rival male love interest. Again... sigh. Give him a ridiculous name. He's the opposite of the main love interest, in both looks and personality. Although he's good-natured and faithful, the MC should treat him like dirt. It's justified because he has a deep, dark secret... he's EVUL.<br /><br />- Remember: the MC and love interest don't need to have anything in common, any respect or genuine feelings for each other, or any charisma. Just make them pant and swoon, talk about how their love is a drug, and kiss once or twice. No sex please, we're prudes!<br /><br />- Copy the Twilight formula (Mary-Sue main character, supernatual love interest with dark secrets, a love triangle with a bad boy and nice guy where the nice guy comes in last, lame villains who show up in the last few chapters), changing it just enough so that no one can accuse you of plagiarism. Write some half-assed paranormal mythology, add some boring side characters, and maybe throw in a few cliched teenage girl fantasy elements taken from any amateur writing site populated mainly by teens - the new hot guy at school is a ROCK STAR, and a supernatural creature too! In fact, he might be the biggest Big Bad supernatural of them all, even if he rarely uses his powers for anything but stalking the MC... Anyway, don't bother to flesh out the fantasy elements in your story. Everyone knows that PR fans read only to fap.<br /><br />- Slam your hand down on the keyboard and write whatever random shit comes to mind. Do not bother to edit your work.<br /><br />- Stir all ingredients together. Optional: bake in a 350 degree oven (i.e. edit) for three weeks. Give to a publisher and insist that this is the "next big thing". Sure, it's the book equivalent of Cheez Whiz, but the audience won't care. They're just dumb teens, right? Wrap the whole mess up in a pretty cover. Serve cold. Warning: may cause indigestion, flatulence, fits of book-throwing rage, heart palpitations, head explosion due to stupid, and death. Not recommended for discerning readers of any age.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I'm done with the whole paranormal romance genre. Seriously. I like fantasy and I like romance, so why can't I find any paranormal romance that isn't made of fail? Think I'm done with self-published works too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17260746533949706428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9649421069146387468" style="display:none">.<br />Well this is really a little bit of not much.<br />But I still enjoyed it despite it's emptiness.<br /><br />Pagan is a damsel in distress<br />There's a lot of telling rather than showing.<br />There's a love triangle and a mean girl thrown in for angst.<br />Nothin' much happens.<br />Hardly any kissing, let alone heavy petting etc. Not like any high school students I remember!<br />And just what is it about pagan, that the two hottest guys in school want her??<br />The song lyrics are just awful. Like something I wrote when I was 10 yr old.<br />...But it's an easy listen and i find myself still listening to find answers, knowing that i prob won't get them until the 2nd book.<br /><b>the book is a tease..</b><br /><br />Pagan is your average high school student. What year? No idea. <br />She is approached by the quarterback and hot guy of her school for tutoring. She's never liked him but maybe her first impressions were wrong??<br />His ex (the head cheerleader of course *sigh*) will be a source of angst throughout the story.<br />Then there's the fact that she can see 'souls' (aka ghosts), mute lost people that wander around. But today she sees a ghost that talks back to her. <br />Is he a soul or something more?<br />I did find the whole triangle irritating. The author tries to suggest why Pagan stays with the OM, but I always thought less of her for that fact. <b>...She's a bit of a twit really...</b><br /><br />It's predictable and well <i>blah blah blah.</i><br /><br />But if you're in the mood for a book that's entertaining in a low angst way and doesn't make you think... this one works well.<br /><br />Pagan will never be my fave heroine. Both her and Dank are rather empty.<br /><br />But dammit, I need to read the next one. <br /><br />Ends on a tentative HFN.<br /><br />safety is good <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don't think he's ever been with a woman before... but in the mean time he uses the evil OW Kendra to... I don't know what...<br />They kiss and dance closely. Pagan kisses Lief and there's a brief groping session on her couch at one point. But it's clear to her (and Dank) that she doesn't care for him like that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The audio reader was good.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_206995749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206995749" />
    <a title="Calia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5918467-calia"><img alt="Calia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530305278p2/5918467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206995749?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calia" href="/user/show/5918467-calia">Calia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5918467-calia?shelf=young-adult-reads">young-adult-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206995749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1163708827775495034">You know <i>those</i> books... The ones that you anxiously wait for. <br/><br/>Come on, you know what I’m talking about..<br/><br/>The premise is great. The cover is amazing! We’ve all seen them. Most of them have girls with dresses that look like they were stolen from <i>“Gone with the Wind”</i> movie set, and have no actual meaning to the book. You then read the book, and sadly your let down. <br/><br/>But <b>Existence</b>... <br/><br/>This book, like the cover, is just... <i>delicious</i>. <br/><br/>I was kinda worried at first. I fell in love with Abbi Glines writing </span>
  <span id="freeText1163708827775495034" style="display:none">You know <i>those</i> books... The ones that you anxiously wait for. <br /><br />Come on, you know what I’m talking about..<br /><br />The premise is great. The cover is amazing! We’ve all seen them. Most of them have girls with dresses that look like they were stolen from <i>“Gone with the Wind”</i> movie set, and have no actual meaning to the book. You then read the book, and sadly your let down. <br /><br />But <b>Existence</b>... <br /><br />This book, like the cover, is just... <i>delicious</i>. <br /><br />I was kinda worried at first. I fell in love with Abbi Glines writing in <b>The Vincent Boys... </b> <br /><i>Moment of silence for Beau, and his hotness</i>..... <br />And it didn’t help that I’ve been on strike from all the paranormal books that are ALL. ALIKE. <br /><br />Existence was a read, IMO, that was <b>new</b> and stood firmly on its on. I didn’t read a scene and think, “Hmm where have I seen that before?” Every part of the book was smoothly put together. <br />Abbi makes nothing “complex”, and the book more complicated than it REALLY has to be. <br /><br />Now to the book description: <br />Pagan Moore is not really your average girl. She sees things that most people wouldn’t her whole life. None of it has really confused her until Dank came into her life. He’s there everywhere she turns... <br /><br />And while she is dealing with all that, she is asked to tutor the hunky Leif Montgomery. When she finally agrees to, she gets to know him. <br />Leif is not what he seems. And Pagan finds out more about his past that shows that he’s more than the school jock, maybe even starts to feel more than the "friend vibe" for him. I think it’s important to mention this because, it alters the book. And alters Pagan’s life.... <br /><br />Before I talk about the MC's. I need to add that I loved <b>all</b> the characters. <br /><br /><b>Pagan</b>. I already like her for her cool name. She was such a fun character, and not only that, she was interesting! I thought she had a heart to her, and was kind to everyone around her. She had a lot of things to me that are a MUST. <br />Very few MC’s possess them, and I’m still trying to figure out why there isn’t more...<br />You have <b>Abby</b> from <i>Beautiful Disaster</i>, <b>Brenna</b> from <i>Double Clutch</i>, and maybe a few more others....<br />So here’s the list: <br />-She isn’t annoying: I didn’t want to toss my laptop at the wall due to her idiotic behavior. <br />-She’s intriguing. <br />-She’s brave. I’ll be completely honest. I’m a wimp. I read this book through the night and there were a few times that I looked around the room to make sure I was good and nothing creepy was there. If I was in Pagan’s situation I would have been using my puffer, and popping back Prozac’s like they were out of style.... <br /><br />And then there’s Leif....<br />Let’s not forget about Dank, either. <i>(I’ll get to the hot piece of death later)</i> <br /><br />I liked Leif.. A LOT. The things you find out about him make him seem human and vulnerable. And we all love vulnerable in a male. So I was drawn to him. I thought at first that there was going to be some sort of love triangle. I’m cautious with those, because I latch onto a certain boy and I usually don’t verve far from that character. <br /><br />I veered off completely, and I’m <b>SO</b> okay with that. <br />Because Dank is...Dank. <br />I know a lot of people are throwing major bitch fits over his name. But come on! I <i>KNOW</i> I'm not the only one who loved it! <br />I like when authors think outside of the "name box" and search for these unique names, such as.. DANK. But I have an odd name myself, so Dank, I have got yo' back brotha'! <br />But there’s no other character I can compare him to. He’s very mysterious. In such an intriguing way. <br />I thought he was dark <i>(well, duh)</i> and was fighting a lot of his feelings when it came to Pagan. Normally, for me, I notice that most authors can’t pull off the bad boy with true feelings. It usually doesn’t “flow” for me. But it worked perfectly! <br /><br />Have I mentioned the tension around these two? No? <br />They have <b>blows-one’s-mind</b> chemistry!! I got the “good” chills a few times when it came to Pagan and Dank. <br />First Ashton and Beau in The Vincent Boys. <br />And now Pagan and Dank. <br />It’s virtually impossible for Ms. Glines to write blandly. Her characters have spark, and staggering tension! <br /><br />I won’t go on any further about Existence.. Partially out of fear that I’ll spill everything, and all the amazing details that I enjoyed reading. <br /><br />Just read it, you’ll love it. <br /><br />But I need to say: <br />The ending... <i>What. the. Crap</i>..... What a cliffhanger.<br />How could you leave me hanging? I’m willing to move past all this and forgive Abbi. <br /><br />Because hopefully (cross ones finger) the second book will be released SOON! <br />My ideal date, and this off the top of my head.....would be next week. But I highly doubt that will happen. Until then, I wait, impatiently......<br /><br />And until then, I know have another great author to catalog in my brain. <br />Abbi Glines writing takes a <b>priority</b>. You might be reading other books (like I was) but you’ll put them away, and store them in the back of your mind JUST so you can read what new world she has created. She’s just <i>that</i> flippin’ good! <br /><br />If you read <i>The Vincent Boys</i> and liked it, then you’re guaranteed to love <b>Existence</b>! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1163708827775495034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_206466203" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206466203" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206466203?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206466203" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14447023187167814993"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/abbi-glines/review-existence.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358516i/709720.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I won't say much about this book as I usually don't review the books I don't like. And surprise-surprise, I didn't quite like it.<br/><br/>Still, I have to get it out of my head, so here it comes.. my review wanna be (or if you wish my bubbling thoughts):<br/><br/>I blame it on the cover!<br/>I hate the fact that this couple is all over the place, on all kind of covers, but still there was something I liked about this one. Probably those eyes, going hand in hand with the book description.<br/>Damn marketing! I should jus</span>
  <span id="freeText14447023187167814993" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/abbi-glines/review-existence.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358516i/709720.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I won't say much about this book as I usually don't review the books I don't like. And surprise-surprise, I didn't quite like it.<br><br>Still, I have to get it out of my head, so here it comes.. my review wanna be (or if you wish my bubbling thoughts):<br><br>I blame it on the cover!<br>I hate the fact that this couple is all over the place, on all kind of covers, but still there was something I liked about this one. Probably those eyes, going hand in hand with the book description.<br>Damn marketing! I should just learn my lesson for once!<br><br>The beginning of the book was really promising - you see, I have a soft spot for witty characters, that have the habit to 'spit' sarcasm every time they open their mouth, and Pagan seemed to be that kind of girl.<br>Also, a love story between a human girl and Death itself sounded like a hell of a story, right?.. Right?!<br>Well, I was at least right about the hell part.<br><br>In the first chapters I loved Pagan and her relationship with Leif - they were so cute together that made me sad thinking about the fact that Leif wasn't Death, so I knew he wasn't <i>the one</i>. Even the first moments with Dank were cute and funny, and most of the times 'cute' is enough for me. I like cute, even though (if I am not mistaken) Pagan wasn't a fan of this word/description - not when defining her anyway.<br><br>Now, not mentioning the choice for the names that put me off faster than blinking, what I didn't like about this book was how, after finally being with Leif (after an incident that made me roll my eyes until I almost saw my back), all Pagan's interest returned and remained on Dank - in an obsessive, hair-pulling kind of way. Talking about love-triangles and how they get to annoy me.. not that it was really a love-triangle anyways.<br>It got from funny, to damn depressing in an instant.<br>Pagan was mostly sad or crying her heart out, and not understanding why Dank wouldn't like her back, and if he did why would he ignore her.. And then, there was <i>that thing</i> with him watching her sleep (which is in fact really creepy, as creepy as it was in all the books before this one. stop using this cliché in books, it is not hot at all, it's just annoying as hell and not original at all!!!!!) and then he was ignoring her even more, and oh.. why would he get involved with the only girl in the world Pagan didn't like, if not to add even more teenage drama to the story. I tell you, hair-pulling.. at that point I just couldn't relate with it at all.<br><br>So.. if you still wish to read this book after me warning you, be my guest, but I would hate to say "I told you so".<br>And if you happen to like it, great for you, I wish I would have liked it better too - I read for pleasure and it pains me not to like a book.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/abbi-glines/review-existence.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TIGixv31tf1kxU3CJtLCVUuiCHkHT7bYSx1yQ++JtmX+XfiO4vCMBYBlV+jk+Bv1BsvX6yHMOEimtLivM6pH9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6OD1r+yyquVs16Z8NaxK1s9y6M2cxlQs+sNmN794zC1aPK/n87eTHYh3vFb3hpN2ghs3X7pF2rwXaqzbY1s9vg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13118773147868716444">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be Britis</span>
  <span id="freeText13118773147868716444" style="display:none">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be British but alas she was born in Alabama. When asked how many books she has written she has to stop and count on her fingers. When she’s not locked away writing, she is reading, shopping (major shoe and purse addiction), sneaking off to the movies alone, and listening to the drama in her teenagers lives while making mental notes on the good stuff to use later. Don’t judge.<br /><br />You can connect with Abbi online in several different ways. She uses social media to procrastinate.<br /></span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
